  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_59292a0b-777e-4368-8ea2-ac2d5e96208e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14855147071311596815"><b>An award-winning novel about growing up and making choices<br/></b><br/>Virginia Euwer Wolff's groundbreaking novel, written in free verse, tells the story of fourteen-year-old LaVaughn, who is determined to go to college--she just needs the money to get there. <br/><br/>When she answers a babysitting ad, LaVaughn meets Jolly, a seventeen-year-old single mother with two kids by different fathers.</span>
  <span id="freeText14855147071311596815" style="display:none"><b>An award-winning novel about growing up and making choices<br /></b><br />Virginia Euwer Wolff's groundbreaking novel, written in free verse, tells the story of fourteen-year-old LaVaughn, who is determined to go to college--she just needs the money to get there. <br /><br />When she answers a babysitting ad, LaVaughn meets Jolly, a seventeen-year-old single mother with two kids by different fathers. As she helps Jolly make lemonade out of the lemons her life has given her, LaVaughn learns some lessons outside the classroom.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_450156216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450156216" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450156216?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590481410" href="/book/show/1218652.Make_Lemonade">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450156216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10166728735951209931">Rating: 4* of five<br/><br/><b>The Book Description</b>: Virginia Euwer Wolff's groundbreaking novel, written in free verse, tells the story of fourteen-year-old LaVaughn, who is determined to go to college--she just needs the money to get there. When she answers a babysitting ad, LaVaughn meets Jolly, a seventeen-year-old single mother with two kids by different fathers. As she helps Jolly make lemonade out of the lemons her life has given her, LaVaughn learns some lessons outside the classroom. With two kids h</span>
  <span id="freeText10166728735951209931" style="display:none">Rating: 4* of five<br /><br /><b>The Book Description</b>: Virginia Euwer Wolff's groundbreaking novel, written in free verse, tells the story of fourteen-year-old LaVaughn, who is determined to go to college--she just needs the money to get there. When she answers a babysitting ad, LaVaughn meets Jolly, a seventeen-year-old single mother with two kids by different fathers. As she helps Jolly make lemonade out of the lemons her life has given her, LaVaughn learns some lessons outside the classroom. With two kids hanging in the balance, they need to make the best out of life -- and they can only do it for themselves and each other. <br /><br /><b>My Review</b>: Okay. Brace yourselves. This is a YA novel written in a teenaged girl's voice in free verse. What does this strongly imply I am about to do? Rant and invectivize and holler, right? As a rule, a safe bet.<br /><br />Rule, meet exception.<br /><br />I love LaVaughn and Jolly and their weird, codependent growing up. I am impressed by the genuineness of all the various lovings going on through the book. I am even overlooking the free-verse affectation. It's totally unnecessary to tell this story in any kind of verse, but whatever. LaVaughn's first person voice is poignantly like that of other young women I've known as they grew up, and makes me mist over a little bit.<br /><br />Quote me on that and I will swear an oath on a stack of Bibles that you're lying.<br /><br />The events that LaVaughn narrates remind me of my many attempts to save others. White knight, in more ways than one, rides in and saves the day...then <i>poof</i> you're invisible when things go right. It's like being a parent!<br /><br />It IS being a parent. And that both sucks and blows. But it's also, in a weird masochistic way, the best feeling of all, because there is one fewer roadblock in someone else's path through life because you, O Savior Complex Haver, gave in and did what your warped sense of self insists is right.<br /><br />Problem is...that warp is there because, more often than not, you ARE right.<br /><br />La Vaughn's in for a long long haul. But she also gets something big in return, something not always obvious at the moment, and often not until a lot of life has passed beneath one's eyes. She gets to know in her heart that at least a few people had one less rock to carry, one more reason to smile, one small moment of being, if not feeling, cared about and for, because she lifted, carried, cared, smiled.<br /><br />Most days that's enough. Come hear her tell about it. It's a good story.	</span>
  <a data-text-id="10166728735951209931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93422721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7608563811515469006">This was a very powerful book for me. It's a novel told in a free verse style, and I wondered if that would bother me. I soon realized, though, that the verse style made the story more powerful. Even though it reads very easily as a novel, it allowed the author to place subtle emphasis on certain words and phrases. I loved it!<br/><br/><i>Make Lemonade</i> is the story of 14-year-old LaVaughn who befriends Jolly, 17-year-old mother of two, when she answers Jolly's ad for a babysitter. It's easy for her to judge </span>
  <span id="freeText7608563811515469006" style="display:none">This was a very powerful book for me. It's a novel told in a free verse style, and I wondered if that would bother me. I soon realized, though, that the verse style made the story more powerful. Even though it reads very easily as a novel, it allowed the author to place subtle emphasis on certain words and phrases. I loved it!<br /><br /><i>Make Lemonade</i> is the story of 14-year-old LaVaughn who befriends Jolly, 17-year-old mother of two, when she answers Jolly's ad for a babysitter. It's easy for her to judge Jolly and the situation she got herself in, but when LaVaughn gets to know more about Jolly, she begins to understand that there is more to Jolly than she first realized.<br /><br />While the story, as seen through LaVaughn's eyes, appears to be about Jolly and her transition into a person who "takes hold," the underlying story is all about LaVaughn. We see her change and develop as she comes to love and care for not just Jolly's children, but Jolly herself. The relationships she builds gives her new perspective and understanding into the world outside herself.<br /><br />The story was beautifully told, and I'm eager to read the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7608563811515469006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46675326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1201237844215516762">Fourteen-year-old LaVaughn answers an ad for an after-school babysitting job that turns out to be life-changing. She cares for the two young children of 17-year-old Jolly, who works second shift at a factory and whose life is a mess. When Jolly gets fired, LaVaughn babysits for free during Jolly's job search. The book is beautiful to read with a poetic style that defies rules and expectations, and tells a provoking story that challenges the reader's assumptions about poverty, teen pregnancy, and</span>
  <span id="freeText1201237844215516762" style="display:none">Fourteen-year-old LaVaughn answers an ad for an after-school babysitting job that turns out to be life-changing. She cares for the two young children of 17-year-old Jolly, who works second shift at a factory and whose life is a mess. When Jolly gets fired, LaVaughn babysits for free during Jolly's job search. The book is beautiful to read with a poetic style that defies rules and expectations, and tells a provoking story that challenges the reader's assumptions about poverty, teen pregnancy, and life choices. <br /><br />This book jerked me out of my comfort zone, but it did not sweep me away to a better place like the plot-driven escapist books I enjoy reading. I didn't sympathize with main character, LaVaughn. She seems too perfect, inhumanly perfect, with no endearing faults. Her only real fault (and it is not endearing) is a tendency to judge others. I found this book depressing, but the writing is beautiful and the story poses some worthwhile questions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1201237844215516762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3215419104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3215419104" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3215419104?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Savannah Porter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Savannah Porter" href="/user/show/25667467-savannah-porter">Savannah Porter</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3215419104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4906481628467141691">This book tells the story of LaVaughn babysitting for a teenage mom with two kids, and helping her land on her feet after she is fired. All the characters in this book seem real and they’re easy to connect to. I liked the free verse format and I felt like it added to LaVaughn’s character voice. I gave this book only three stars because I felt some emotional impact was missing. Sure, it was sad and hopeful, but I wanted to feel more. Perhaps I didn’t because it ends so abruptly (though I guess th</span>
  <span id="freeText4906481628467141691" style="display:none">This book tells the story of LaVaughn babysitting for a teenage mom with two kids, and helping her land on her feet after she is fired. All the characters in this book seem real and they’re easy to connect to. I liked the free verse format and I felt like it added to LaVaughn’s character voice. I gave this book only three stars because I felt some emotional impact was missing. Sure, it was sad and hopeful, but I wanted to feel more. Perhaps I didn’t because it ends so abruptly (though I guess the ending was more realistic to life), or LaVaughn and Jolly’s relationship never really progressed to friendship, or it felt more like a snapshot of life rather than a well-constructed story. But it was still a good read, and I’d recommend it to any middle grader, teen, or even adult—it serves as a great window or mirror to being a teen mom.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4906481628467141691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8830421-j-l-s-bibliomania?shelf=z-2016-reads">z-2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8830421-j-l-s-bibliomania?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8830421-j-l-s-bibliomania?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8830421-j-l-s-bibliomania?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8830421-j-l-s-bibliomania?shelf=books-in-verse">books-in-verse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774137178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16047788940609820669">While a nice enough story about resilience, Make Lemonade confirmed that I just don't "get" the whole novel in free verse phenomenon. <br/> <br/>Sometimes limits, such as the compressed length of a short story, or the structured poetry of Shakespeare's plays lead to increased creativity on the part of the author. As I have for the other verse novels I've read I felt like the poetry in Make Lemonade led to lack of complexity in characterization and material closer to a short story than a "novel". </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16990924199270633606" style="display:none"> This book is about how a mom(Jolly) who's seventeen and has two kids, is helped by thirteen-year-old LaVaughn, and she turns out to be one of the most important assets in Jolly's life. It's very focused on the topic that the book is about. A lot of moments in this book were very good. <br /> There was one part of Make Lemonade that really cuaght my eye.That was when Jolly did everything she could to save her baby, Jillie. She did CPR and mouth-to-mouth all the way untill the ambulance came. I think that is truly showing love for her baby, even though she's only seventeen. </span>

<div id="review_458987453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458987453" />
    <a title="Christine Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14718852-christine-kim"><img alt="Christine Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353303932p2/14718852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458987453?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine Kim" href="/user/show/14718852-christine-kim">Christine Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458987453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13172539035115694563">Make Lemonade Book Review <br/><br/>LaVaughn is an ambitious girl with high hopes and dreams of going to college. She studies hard in school, gets good grades, and does her best to earn money for college. However, LaVaughn ends up babysitting Jolly’s two kids, and Jolly is a single mom who is 17 years old, struggling fiercely with life. LaVaughn is determined to show Jolly and her kids that life isn’t always sour and that a world full of sweet delights still exists. The time the four people spend with eac</span>
  <span id="freeText13172539035115694563" style="display:none">Make Lemonade Book Review <br /><br />LaVaughn is an ambitious girl with high hopes and dreams of going to college. She studies hard in school, gets good grades, and does her best to earn money for college. However, LaVaughn ends up babysitting Jolly’s two kids, and Jolly is a single mom who is 17 years old, struggling fiercely with life. LaVaughn is determined to show Jolly and her kids that life isn’t always sour and that a world full of sweet delights still exists. The time the four people spend with each other is not always full of happiness but they bond with one another and soon come to love each other like family.<br />I liked Make Lemonade because it showed much about what life is worth fighting for and it gave me hope. The way LaVaughn encouraged Jolly and her kids, the way Jolly didn’t give up on her life, which seemed hopeless, touched me and taught me an important lesson. Things aren’t going to be sour and bitter forever; there is a time when things come to an end, when things will become sweet.<br />This book related to my life (well, it related more to my past) because when I first moved here to Korea, I struggled with Korean culture and education. School did not seem like a place of learning and I had almost given up hope. But, by God’s grace, I was accepted into YISS after two and a half years. I was overjoyed because I could finally see hope and hold on to it. This was what God had planned for me. Now, I am still adjusting to the American way of education, but I am extremely thankful for my present situation.<br />I would recommend this book to people who are currently in unfortunate positions. For example, I would introduce this book to a girl orphan and maybe she could relate to the characters. Or a struggling single mother who might read this book would definitely understand what Jolly went through. But Make Lemonade is still a book that anyone and everyone can read. <br />This book may not have the perfect smell of peaches and cream, but its tangy and homely scent is sure to attract readers as bees are to honey.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13172539035115694563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14313153687751974631" style="display:none">What an incredible book!!!! It is rich in character development, spot on in the harsh reality of the consequences of teen aged pregnancy when there is little or no support base, poetic in words and heartbreaking and heartwarming at the same time!<br /><br />Needing a job to save for college, 14 year old LaVaughn accepts the position of babysitter for two children. Seventeen years old, living in poverty, surrounded by hopelessness, their mother Jolly simply cannot get a grip on how to survive and look beyond day - day living. Her rent isn't paid, there is little food, and her children need clothing.<br /><br />Kind heartedly, LaVaughn attempts to set Jolly on the path leading to a future, while struggling to learn the difference between a helping hand, a hand out and the trickiness of being pulled under.<br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>

  <span id="freeText16722485645592003328" style="display:none">I haven't reviewed any YA on GR yet, not because I've not read any, but there's so much YA that covers all the same territory (i.e. dysfunction) in much the same way. Eminem's first CD came out in 1996. Poetry slams and hip hop have since become youth's mainstream. <br /><br />But, if this book wasn't good, if it didn't hit a nerve, if it didn't resonate with both its targeted audience and those who get these books into kids hands, I wouldn't be writing this review now, twenty years later. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8815084621332301860">5 stars not just because it's excellent ... because it is ... but because Wolff really was at the leading edge of what has become a delightful genre with all kinds of wonderful possibilities--the novel in verse. I find it interesting that Wolff knew instinctively that this style of writing (which didn't even have a name at the time) would be the perfect format to address bright but struggling readers. Telescoped ideas and emotions, viscerally expressed themes; that's what this genre does best, a</span>
  <span id="freeText8815084621332301860" style="display:none">5 stars not just because it's excellent ... because it is ... but because Wolff really was at the leading edge of what has become a delightful genre with all kinds of wonderful possibilities--the novel in verse. I find it interesting that Wolff knew instinctively that this style of writing (which didn't even have a name at the time) would be the perfect format to address bright but struggling readers. Telescoped ideas and emotions, viscerally expressed themes; that's what this genre does best, and the best novels in verse published today are still those that compress a lot of meaning into surprisingly few words.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8815084621332301860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText13623840346158551263" style="display:none">I liked the book Make Lemonade by Virginia Euwef Wolff because it’s about a girl close to my age. First of all, Jolly needed a baby sitter because she had work. A girl Lavaughn offered to watch her kids. In the middle jolly loses her job and doesn't know what to do. Lavaughn helps with the kids still, and jolly has to go to school to get a better job and support her kids. I liked it when Lavaughn tells her mom, “Jollys fired that means I’ve got no babysitting money”(Wolf.60) her mom feels bad for jolly and tried to help. This is one of my favorite parts because her mom is doing the right thing and helping Jolly. I also like it when Lavaughn “Took Jolly to her steam class”(Wolf.86). Lavaughn is trying to shoe Jolly that she needs to get back in school so she can support her kids now and in the future. Others may think that 17 year olds shouldn't have kids and a house so they might not want teens to read it. However, It's that person's life and they can do what they want when they want. In conclusion, I would rate it 4 stars out of 5. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText7262333082388874111" style="display:none">There’s a girl, and babysits for a women named Jolly. Her house is usually a mess too. Then Jolly loses her job and the girl convinces her to go back to school. She ends up back at school just as the girl wanted. Jolly then tries to contact a billionaire to see if he can help her out with her financial struggles.<br />It uses the figurative device of imagery. You felt like you were struggling with Jolly in her trials. There is a very special connection between the reader and Jolly in this book. You can really feel the panic that everyone else is in too during the story. You can feel the heat of the moment.<br />I thought that the book was super good and I personally really enjoyed it. I recommend it to anyone who likes a good story. I really liked the characters, they were all fun and relatable. I hope that I can find more books like this. Definitely a must read for those who like poetry.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14571514002230859760">The characters and story revealed in these pages are ones that will be recognizable/lived by many and a revelation to others. The voice in this writing is mentor text for authenticity and organic lyricism. I recently reread OUT OF THE DUST (Karen Hesse), which is written with such realism in the pervasive, choking, devastating dust of the 1930s Plains states. In very word I could feel, taste, experience the diminishment and hopelessness of their reality, all the while craving a glass of clean wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14571514002230859760" style="display:none">The characters and story revealed in these pages are ones that will be recognizable/lived by many and a revelation to others. The voice in this writing is mentor text for authenticity and organic lyricism. I recently reread OUT OF THE DUST (Karen Hesse), which is written with such realism in the pervasive, choking, devastating dust of the 1930s Plains states. In very word I could feel, taste, experience the diminishment and hopelessness of their reality, all the while craving a glass of clean water and a shower. <br />In MAKE LEMONADE the author accomplishes something similar, embedding the gritty, sticky reality of Jolly's struggle while building a relationship among the characters and with the reader that demanded acceptance and embrace. "Unflinching" is the word that comes to mind, but not because the story is harsh, rather because it is so very tender and honest. <br />Several titles follow these characters forward in time, and I will be reading them soon.</span>

<div id="review_2022162914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2022162914" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1695996-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330713544p2/1695996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2022162914?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/1695996-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590481410" href="/book/show/1218652.Make_Lemonade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1695996-danielle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1695996-danielle?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1695996-danielle?shelf=in-verse">in-verse</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2022162914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9170135465869991586">I like LaVaughn. I like the way she tries to figure out the world, if she's taking advantage of Jolly or if Jolly is taking advantage of her. I like the way these two girls, only three years apart, have such vastly different lives and they way they're brought together. I like that there isn't anything too trite like a scene where LaVaughn just gives in an cleans Jolly's apartment for her (which is what I might have done). <br/><br/>I enjoyed the sequel, True Believer, even more. I think the poetic style c</span>
  <span id="freeText9170135465869991586" style="display:none">I like LaVaughn. I like the way she tries to figure out the world, if she's taking advantage of Jolly or if Jolly is taking advantage of her. I like the way these two girls, only three years apart, have such vastly different lives and they way they're brought together. I like that there isn't anything too trite like a scene where LaVaughn just gives in an cleans Jolly's apartment for her (which is what I might have done). <br /><br />I enjoyed the sequel, True Believer, even more. I think the poetic style comes through more there, reminds me a bit of Sharon Creech.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9170135465869991586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2596289283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5204023174911668916">This book was about a teenage girl named LaVaughn who just wanted to have a job to save money for college. However, then she meets Jolly, a girl not that much older than her who has 2 kids. Jolly is struggling and the LaVaughn is helping her out by babysitting. This book was definitely a page turner and I loved this story.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3277817493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3277817493" />
    <a title="Dani Castro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109514341-dani-castro"><img alt="Dani Castro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580466921p2/109514341.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3277817493?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani Castro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani Castro" href="/user/show/109514341-dani-castro">Dani Castro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3277817493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4531219547542898713">If I could give a 3.5 I would. Make Lemonade is about LaVaughn, 14, she babysits for 17 year-old Jolly, who is a single mom. LaVaughn seems to have her life together, but when she gets involved in Jolly's life the story turns into one of friendship, parenthood, responsibility, and the opportunities life can throw at us when we don't give up. Race is not included in this story and I thought that was a great addition. I'm happy about the ending. I thought it was realistic. This book is a good read</span>
  <span id="freeText4531219547542898713" style="display:none">If I could give a 3.5 I would. Make Lemonade is about LaVaughn, 14, she babysits for 17 year-old Jolly, who is a single mom. LaVaughn seems to have her life together, but when she gets involved in Jolly's life the story turns into one of friendship, parenthood, responsibility, and the opportunities life can throw at us when we don't give up. Race is not included in this story and I thought that was a great addition. I'm happy about the ending. I thought it was realistic. This book is a good ready for young women, but it may be tough to get through, despite being kind of easy. It may not be the most fun read in a market with so much variety in the YA section. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SDwDfrHVX07OkXsQlw+YspGi0jHmBpInrmlgGJIFeYzXzODSv3AEoueCgyOA6xvU9B+USWvh1lUkgMB8/V86jw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SkQssFB8cJMqb9PjGwqzaVtEW8xmBH9P3v8dop/ZNZHVtM8cXtkrfwN8K9AM7jAPPvkdtOvjOz1UFr3G8IN2kg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9844.Virginia_Euwer_Wolff">About Virginia Euwer Wolff</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9844.Virginia_Euwer_Wolff"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1209044403p3/9844.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9575627092716282174">On August 25th, Virginia Euwer Wolff was born in Portland, Oregon. Her family lived on an apple and pear orchard near Mount Hood. Her father died when she was five years old and she admits her childhood was pretty messed up, but she held things together with her violin. She graduated from Smith College. She raised a son and daughter before going back to teaching high school English. <br/>She was almost</span>
  <span id="freeText9575627092716282174" style="display:none">On August 25th, Virginia Euwer Wolff was born in Portland, Oregon. Her family lived on an apple and pear orchard near Mount Hood. Her father died when she was five years old and she admits her childhood was pretty messed up, but she held things together with her violin. She graduated from Smith College. She raised a son and daughter before going back to teaching high school English. <br />She was almost fifty years old when she started writing children books. Virginia thought she might have one or two good books in her before the end but that was proven wrong. Today, she is no longer teaching, but writes full-time.<br /><br />When Wolff was asked why she writes for kids and not grown-ups, She responded, "Because I don't think I have a handle on how to write for grown-ups. The grown-up publishing world is so fraught with one-upsmanship, scorn and snobbery. I did write an adult novel. Thank goodness it went out of print. I think we kids' authors still start out with hope every morning. We honor our audience."<br /><br />Ms. Wolff has received many awards for her works, which include the Golden Kite Award for Fiction for her book Make Lemonade, the ALA Notable Book for Children for The Mozart Season and many, many others.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/virginiaeuwerwolff">http://us.macmillan.com/author/virgin...</a></span>
